  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_fd285fb7-2bb0-4d8a-a712-ec23a78d0e84'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText10574529391041632899" style="display:none">"You must never do anything that might expose our secret. This means that, in general, you cannot form close bonds with humans. You can speak to us, and you can always commune with the Ocean, but you are deadly to humans. You are, essentially, a weapon. A very beautiful weapon. I won't lie to you, it can be a lonely existence, but once you are done, you get to live. All you have to give, for now, is obedience and time..."<br /><br />The same speech has been given hundreds of times to hundreds of beautiful girls who enter the sisterhood of sirens. Kahlen has lived by these rules for years now, patiently waiting for the life she can call her own. But when Akinli, a human, enters her world, she can't bring herself to live by the rules anymore. Suddenly the life she's been waiting for doesn't seem nearly as important as the one she's living now.</span>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/641791-my-11-year-old-daughter-wants-to-read">My 11-year-old daughter wants to read this. I don&#39;t mind her reading many young adult books, including ones with romance, but I&#39;m not keen on her reading ones where the love scenes are quite explicit (as far as Young Adult goes). She&#39;s read The Hunger Games, the Matched series, and If I Stay with my approval, just to give an idea of what I&#39;m okay with. Any thoughts about this one?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_641791'><a id="like_count_community_question_641791" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/641791?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">7 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F6618272-the-siren">like</a></span>

<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/34487436-st-gerard-expectant-mothers"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1600272409i/34487436._UY100_CR38,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/34487436-st-gerard-expectant-mothers">St. Gerard Expectant Mothers</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Nothing objectionable even for savvy 11 year olds. It's pretty cheesy but enjoyable and the teen romance element is really underplayed. However, it is<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Nothing objectionable even for savvy 11 year olds. It's pretty cheesy but enjoyable and the teen romance element is really underplayed. However, it is going with idea of death and the siren mythology of sending humans to their deaths. That is something you might want to consider when allowing her to read it.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=sisterhood">sisterhood</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=soul-mates">soul-mates</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=death">death</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1597806504" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5855804132631873315"><br/><strong>Kahlen was supposed to die.</strong><br/><br/>Instead, she has been sentenced to a hundred years of murder.<br/><br/>She was a human, but now she is a siren: <strong>deadly but irresistible</strong>. Her voice is poison, death. When She’s hungry, the Ocean calls for Kahlen and her sisters to use their singing to drown humans. Kahlen has been doing this for eighty years. She doesn’t age or get sick. And while she never relishes in stealing lives, she never dares disobey the Ocean.<br/><br/>Until she meets Akinli.<br/><br/>They weren’t supposed to meet, and she </span>
  <span id="freeText5855804132631873315" style="display:none"><br /><strong>Kahlen was supposed to die.</strong><br /><br />Instead, she has been sentenced to a hundred years of murder.<br /><br />She was a human, but now she is a siren: <strong>deadly but irresistible</strong>. Her voice is poison, death. When She’s hungry, the Ocean calls for Kahlen and her sisters to use their singing to drown humans. Kahlen has been doing this for eighty years. She doesn’t age or get sick. And while she never relishes in stealing lives, she never dares disobey the Ocean.<br /><br />Until she meets Akinli.<br /><br />They weren’t supposed to meet, and she wasn’t supposed to fall in love with him. They can’t be together – yet, Kahlen is bewitched, and even the Ocean can’t keep her away from the only boy who <strong>seems to see past her beauties</strong>.<br /><br />Alright, I know. I know how this may look to you. You may think – not again! Not another clichéd story focused on the soul mates concept!<br /><br /><strong>Come on, you know <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2987125.Kiera_Cass" title="Kiera Cass" rel="nofollow noopener">Kiera Cass</a> doesn’t do eye-roll worthy.</strong><br /><br />There are two things you need to know:<br /><br />First, this is <em>not</em> a retelling of The Little Mermaid. It really, really isn’t, so if that’s what you’re expecting from this, there’s no doubt that you’ll be disappointed.<br /><br />Second, while the blurb gives the illusion of it, the story is <strong>not inundated with romance</strong>.<br /><br />Of course her meeting Akinli is the catalyst, but <strong>everything that comes after plunges us into new themes</strong>, such as motherhood, sisterhood and self-discovery.<br /><br />Kahlen is the Ocean’s favorite. To Kahlen, the Ocean is like a mother to her, and the latter loves Kahlen as if she were her own daughter.<br /><br />The Ocean is definitely a <strong>villain-ish bodiless being in the story</strong>, but it’s still hard to hate Her. She doesn’t like taking human lives and definitely cares about Her sirens. Sometimes She’s despicable, but other times you can’t help but feel pity for Her, as surprising as this may sound.<br /><br />Kahlen’s sisters are everything to her. They live together and <strong>keep one another from breaking apart</strong>. Now that she’s met Akinli, she needs her sisters' support more than ever, since she doesn’t think she can live without him much longer.<br /><br />What makes this book less clichéd is Kahlen’s trying. She tries for months and months to stay far away from him and let him live a normal and human life. And it doesn’t feel forced, or for the sake of the plot: it feels real, because he’s her first love.<br /><br />Throughout the process of finding ways to be with her loved one, she also finds herself. She’s always been the obedient one, but she slowly realizes that the Ocean may not at all times be right and that’s she’s ready to climb mountains for Akinli.<br /><br />Akinli is just so friendly and guileless that I couldn’t stop myself from continuously mentally smiling at him when he was around – <strong>which isn’t that often</strong>.<br /><br />We also have back stories on the sisters – how their lives were before becoming sirens – and I thought that added deepness to the story. Plus their love for Kahlen brightens the atmosphere of the story.<br /><br /><strong>Regardless of the killing part, to me, reading this book was like watching a Disney movie.</strong><br /><br /><strong>Utterly magical.</strong><br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="5855804132631873315" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1556776354" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1556776354" />
    <a title="Claudia Ramírez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13061577-claudia-ram-rez"><img alt="Claudia Ramírez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533869692p2/13061577.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1556776354?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claudia Ramírez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claudia Ramírez" href="/user/show/13061577-claudia-ram-rez">Claudia Ramírez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062391995" href="/book/show/25817407-the-siren">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13061577-claudia-ram-rez?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13061577-claudia-ram-rez?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1556776354" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17745250002794827659">All in all, I liked this book, it was fresh, cute and a fast read, and that's what I needed (because I've been reading heartbreaking, sad books). That said... it was not what I expected. In good ways and in bad ways. Let's start with something I'm not sure if I liked or not, but it sure had me intrigued: The Ocean.<br/><br/>I really liked Her sometimes, but there were other times that She just confused me. I mean, I liked the idea, I think that She was the strongest character of the book, and it's the fir</span>
  <span id="freeText17745250002794827659" style="display:none">All in all, I liked this book, it was fresh, cute and a fast read, and that's what I needed (because I've been reading heartbreaking, sad books). That said... it was not what I expected. In good ways and in bad ways. Let's start with something I'm not sure if I liked or not, but it sure had me intrigued: The Ocean.<br /><br />I really liked Her sometimes, but there were other times that She just confused me. I mean, I liked the idea, I think that She was the strongest character of the book, and it's the first time I read something like it. Her relationship with the girls was one of my favorite aspects of the story, it was very motherly. <br /><br />Akinli was another character I really enjoyed reading, he was just too sweet, caring and funny. I just wish we had more of him in the book. Also! I liked that I thought I knew how his story would end and NOPE! Kiera really surprised me this time :P. I'm not saying I loved the way it ended, but it took me by surprise! Definitely not the cliché I was expecting.<br /><br />Now let's talk about Kahlen... I kinda like her, but not so much. I'm in a point of my life were I can't stand characters whose only aspiration in life is to get married. I also feel that she was unfair with her sisters most of the time... and half of the book she was just bitter and depressed. Blah...<br /><br />Hmmm what else? Oh! THE INSTA LOVE. I mean, it wasn't exactly insta love, but it happened way too fast! I can accept that she instantly had a crush in Akinli (I mean, I would've, too!)... but then in one day she was suddenly in love. What. THEY WERE CUTE TOGETHER! But I'm not a fan of the whole "soulmates" thing when is not well developed :/... <br /><br />That's everything I got to say (for now). I enjoyed the book, the ending felt satisfying, but that's all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17745250002794827659" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" href="/user/show/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee">Mikee (ReadWithMikee)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062391995" href="/book/show/25817407-the-siren">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1371303832" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3305607814410664373">The Siren was a... <b>
  <i>SNOOZEFEST.</i>
</b><br/><br/>I'm so disappointed in this book. I was such a huge fan of The Selection series so I expected to really like The Siren but honestly, everything was just super <b>dull.</b><br/><br/>The characters were boring. The only thing I enjoyed about the siren sisters was their dedication and loyalty to one another. The concept behind the Sirens and the Ocean was interesting but I didn't really love it. And on top of that, the romance was <b>100 percent insta-love.</b> Their feelings developed to</span>
  <span id="freeText3305607814410664373" style="display:none">The Siren was a... <b>
  <i>SNOOZEFEST.</i>
</b><br /><br />I'm so disappointed in this book. I was such a huge fan of The Selection series so I expected to really like The Siren but honestly, everything was just super <b>dull.</b><br /><br />The characters were boring. The only thing I enjoyed about the siren sisters was their dedication and loyalty to one another. The concept behind the Sirens and the Ocean was interesting but I didn't really love it. And on top of that, the romance was <b>100 percent insta-love.</b> Their feelings developed too fast after just one date that lasted for about an hour and because of that, it became way too unrealistic for me and I couldn't even feel any of the <b>
  <u>emotions</u>
</b> that I was supposed to feel in the end.<br /><br />Prior to reading the book, I thought the negative reviews were just a little harsh and I expected that the book would actually improve by a long shot once Kiera Cass <b>rewrote and republished</b> it again, but if I thought this <b>
  <i>"new and improved"</i>
</b> version was ehhh, I could only imagine how the first edition must've been.<br /><br />The only thing that really saved this book for me was the last 50 pages or so but even then, 50 pages doesn't nearly make up for the other disappointing 250.<br /><br />Long story short, reading The Siren felt like a Disney Little Mermaid <b>
  <i>knockoff.</i>
</b> The only difference was that Disney actually pulled off the insta-love romance.<br /><br />Although this book fell short for me, I'm still a <b>
  <u>huge fan</u>
</b> of Kiera Cass. I love her writing and the concepts that she comes up with. Hopefully she comes out with a new book outside of The Selection series to make up for this one because you can always count on me to pick up a book by Kiera Cass.</span>

<div id="review_1462524599" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1462524599" />
    <a title="Trina (Between Chapters)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9323164-trina-between-chapters"><img alt="Trina (Between Chapters)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530495507p2/9323164.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1462524599?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trina (Between Chapters)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trina (Between Chapters)" href="/user/show/9323164-trina-between-chapters">Trina (Between Chapters)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062391995" href="/book/show/25817407-the-siren">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=best-of-swoon">best-of-swoon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=supernaturals">supernaturals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=2016-favorites">2016-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9323164-trina-between-chapters?shelf=standalones">standalones</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1462524599" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11143876363189377508">Please do yourself 2 favors:<br/>1. Do not avoid this book simply because you hated Cass's The Selection series. The two are nothing, nothing, nothing alike. The characters, the world, the writing tone are all so very different. Sure, you may still dislike this one for any number of reasons, but if you're interested in the premise, don't judge it based on a totally separate book series.<br/><br/>2. Do not avoid this book simply because mushy romances aren't your thing. Yes, there is a romance, and that's very </span>
  <span id="freeText11143876363189377508" style="display:none">Please do yourself 2 favors:<br />1. Do not avoid this book simply because you hated Cass's The Selection series. The two are nothing, nothing, nothing alike. The characters, the world, the writing tone are all so very different. Sure, you may still dislike this one for any number of reasons, but if you're interested in the premise, don't judge it based on a totally separate book series.<br /><br />2. Do not avoid this book simply because mushy romances aren't your thing. Yes, there is a romance, and that's very much a big part of the story but there is also SO MUCH MORE. And it's actually more of a tragic tale that I expected.<br /><br />This is a story about many types of love. Sisterly love. Friendship. Parental love. Learning to love yourself. (Love for cake.) And yes, romantic love too. This is one of the best romances I've read in a long time, which is ironic because the love interest appears in less than a quarter of the book total, but what I really took away from this book was all the other kinds of love. Especially the parental love. The parent in this book is the Ocean. She is very much a character in this story and the way in which she loves her Siren daughters is so reminiscent of a mother trying to hold on to her growing children. <br /><br />I'm struggling with wording this next part (thanks brain), but I also want to point out that although this book in no way felt like it was dealing with religion, I got a sense of some religious symbolism. I believe Cass is Christian, so I wondered if maybe the Ocean was meant to be a personification (naturification?) of God. There are definitely many traits of the Ocean that aren't Biblical, but it was a parallel that I saw and it hit me on an emotional level. Any symbolism you may or may not personally see reflected in the Ocean aside, the way in which Cass brought to a life a character that in this world was a type of deity and creator full of undying and jealous love was simply astounding.<br /><br />There are a few more things I want readers to know about this story that make it really awesome.<br />-The main characters are college age, which is refreshing.<br />-The fantasy element of this world was VERY fleshed out. Siren mythology is not a backdrop, it's heavily involved in the story.<br />-The love interest was a good guy. A very believable, kind guy. A nice break from the over abundance of bad boys in YA and NA.<br /><br />And to be fair, here are some things that might turn you off.<br />-There is a heavy dose of instalove. I can hear most of you groaning. But this was the most convincing case of instalove I have ever seen and the reason for that comes down to the fact that these characters didn't spend every waking moment together with their feelings being clouded by being so wrapped up in each other. For the story being told here, it felt fitting.<br />- I don't even have another point here. But having only one point looked weird. Hi.<br /><br />Overall, it's a simple and yet very powerful story that I think would appeal to readers young and old alike.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11143876363189377508" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1549298589" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1549298589" />
    <a title="elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51318038-elena"><img alt="elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605725028p2/51318038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1549298589?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="elena" href="/user/show/51318038-elena">elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062391995" href="/book/show/25817407-the-siren">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1549298589" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15259872895240058935"><blockquote>
  <i>❝Sometimes you have to give the hurt a noise and let it out. If you don’t, it fills you up with its emptiness.❞</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I hate to say it, but I don't think I would read another novel by Kiera Cass. If she did write something else, I don't think I would bother reading it or trying at least. Even if it would be something totally different than her Selection series, I don't think I would give it a shot. They're cute and small and I really like how Kiera makes it enjoyable at times, but other than that, </span>
  <span id="freeText15259872895240058935" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>❝Sometimes you have to give the hurt a noise and let it out. If you don’t, it fills you up with its emptiness.❞</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />I hate to say it, but I don't think I would read another novel by Kiera Cass. If she did write something else, I don't think I would bother reading it or trying at least. Even if it would be something totally different than her Selection series, I don't think I would give it a shot. They're cute and small and I really like how Kiera makes it enjoyable at times, but other than that, I don't enjoy them fully. I only completely loved and enjoyed The One, and the rest were okay stories for me. The Heir and The Crown were not novels I enjoyed, and I was glad I said goodbye to the world of The Selection.<br /><br />Kiera can make others laugh and smile because her writing is cute and quirky and sometimes considered like fan fiction writing, but I am not the biggest fan of it. As some may know, I enjoyed the first 3 books of The Selection and some know, like I said, The One was my favorite. After that, nothing was surprising or gripping in any way. <br /><br />In <i>The Siren</i>, there was really no difference. I was bored most of the time and I didn't bother paying much attention to what was happening. I was tired and didn't care about the romance or whatever these mermaids and the ocean had to do with the main character. It's, I guess, a fantasy novel set in the ocean where the main character turns into a siren and has to keep her voice and identity hidden. I was laughing at times because of the cheesy scenes there were with the main character and her sisters, other sirens, and the boy she was falling in love with, trying to keep her voice muted for the most time or things would turn out bad.<br /><br />The romance felt unrealistic and was also very boring. Nothing happened in the end and everything came to an end so quick. I was actually expecting something to not work out for a while and to be fixed in a different way. I was disappointed in how it ended and how both characters actually met. She completely fell in love with her "love interest" quick. What's his name? Akalini? Aklini? Oh it's Akinli. I think that's his name. And her name is Kahlen? Kiera knows how to come up with interesting and unique names actually. Anyways, the romance was dull, boring and insta-lovish with her mostly. She completely fell for him and wanted to see him again even when she couldn't talk to him. Their moments weren't cute and I thought the whole "I can't talk but I can write down my answers" was silly and laughable.<br /><br />I did enjoy the friendship and relationship between the sisters though. I was glad they were those kind of sisters that understand each other and are there for each other. I didn't get the whole Ocean thing. Her name was always capitalized and she was considered a queen I guess and when she would be called, it was like calling God a Her. It wasn't confusing and nothing from the plot was confusing but rather boring. I've completely ignored negative reviews unless most are saying some elements and aspects that were a little "joyful and enjoying" when others completely hated this. I'm not the biggest fan of Kiera, but I'm glad I've read all her books and enjoyed most of them and just giving them all a shot. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15259872895240058935" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1485693171" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1485693171" />
    <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani"><img alt="Ahmad Sharabiani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194930432p2/614778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1485693171?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahmad Sharabiani" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani">Ahmad Sharabiani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=21th-century">21th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=united-states">united-states</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=literature">literature</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1485693171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5140737928447648590">The Siren, Kiera Cass<br/><br/>A sweeping stand-alone fantasy romance from Kiera Cass, author of the Selection series. <br/><br/>Kahlen is a Siren—bound to serve the Ocean by luring humans to their watery graves with her voice, which is deadly to any human who hears it. <br/><br/><i>"You must never do anything that might expose our secret. This means that, in general, you cannot form close bonds with humans. You can speak to us, and you can always commune with the Ocean, but you are deadly to humans. You are, essentially, a wea</i></span>
  <span id="freeText5140737928447648590" style="display:none">The Siren, Kiera Cass<br /><br />A sweeping stand-alone fantasy romance from Kiera Cass, author of the Selection series. <br /><br />Kahlen is a Siren—bound to serve the Ocean by luring humans to their watery graves with her voice, which is deadly to any human who hears it. <br /><br /><i>"You must never do anything that might expose our secret. This means that, in general, you cannot form close bonds with humans. You can speak to us, and you can always commune with the Ocean, but you are deadly to humans. You are, essentially, a weapon. A very beautiful weapon. I won't lie to you, it can be a lonely existence, but once you are done, you get to live. All you have to give, for now, is obedience and time..."</i> <br /><br />The same speech has been given hundreds of times to hundreds of beautiful girls who enter the sisterhood of sirens. Kahlen has lived by these rules for years now, patiently waiting for the life she can call her own. But when Akinli, a human, enters her world, she can't bring herself to live by the rules anymore. Suddenly the life she's been waiting for doesn't seem nearly as important as the one she's living now.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز بیستم ماه آوریل سال 2018 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: پری دریایی؛ نویسنده: کایرا کاس؛ تهران، نشر باژ؛ مترجم: رباب پورعسگر؛ دبیر مجموعه: نیما کهندانی؛ 1398؛ در 310ص؛ شابک 9786222190552؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان امریکایی - سده 20م<br /><br />اقیانوس در طول عصرهای متمادی، گاه، دختران جوان را از غرق ‌شدن نجات داده؛ این دختران برای جبران محبت اقیانوس، باید صد سال به‌ عنوان پری دریایی به او خدمت کنند؛ در این مدت، زیبایی و جوانی‌شان دست‌ نخورده می‌مانَد، و با صدای مرگ‌بارشان انسان‌ها را اغوا کرده، و به سوی گورستان دریایی می‌کشانند؛ پری‌های دریایی، برای پنهان ‌نگهداشتن ذات واقعی‌شان، هرگز نباید با انسان‌ها حرف بزنند، و نباید به مدتی طولانی در مکانی اقامت کنند.؛ وقتی دوره‌ ی خدمت‌شان در اقیانوس به پایان برسد، فرصتی برای آغازی دوباره، شانسی برای سپری ‌کردن زندگی‌شان به ‌عنوان فردی فانی که از آن‌ها گرفته شده، به آن‌ها اعطا می‌شود؛ «کِیلن»، چندین دهه ‌ی پیش، وقتی خانواده‌ اش در حادثه ‌ای وحشتناک، در آب دریا غرق شدند، تبدیل به یک پری دریایی شد؛ با اینکه اگر کلمه ‌ای به زبان می‌آورد، باعث کشته ‌شدن دیگران می‌شد، ولی نمی‌توانست در مقابل وسوسه‌ ی سپری‌کردن زمانش روی خشکی، تماشای افراد عادی، و اشتیاقش برای روزهایی که بتواند دوباره حرف بزند، بخندد، و آزادانه بین انسان‌ها، زندگی کند، پایداری کند؛ «کِیلن» تسلیم شده بود، تا محکومیتش را، در انزوا بگذراند...؛ تا اینکه «اِیکینلی» را میبیند؛ «اِیکینلی» خوش‌قیافه، و مهربان، همان کسی ست که «کیلن» همیشه رؤیایش را، در سر می‌پرورانده؛ با اینکه «کِیلن» نمی‌تواند با او حرف بزند، ولی خیلی زود، رابطه ‌ای بین‌شان ایجاد می‌شود، که هیچکدام نمی‌توانند آن را انکار کنند...؛ و «کیلن» نمی‌خواهد که انکارش کند؛ عاشقِ یک انسان ‌شدن، یعنی زیر پا گذاشتن همه‌ ی قوانین اقیانوس، و اگر اقیانوس بویی از احساسات «کیلن» ببرد، او مجبور می‌شود، «اِیکینلی» را برای همیشه ترک کند؛ اما «کیلن» برای اولین‌بار در عمرش، که همیشه مطیع قوانین بود، مصمم است به حرف دلش گوش بدهد؛<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 03/06/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>
  <a data-text-id="5140737928447648590" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1458296831" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1458296831" />
    <a title="Wren (fablesandwren)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42780417-wren-fablesandwren"><img alt="Wren (fablesandwren)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596719528p2/42780417.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1458296831?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wren (fablesandwren)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wren (fablesandwren)" href="/user/show/42780417-wren-fablesandwren">Wren (fablesandwren)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062391995" href="/book/show/25817407-the-siren">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42780417-wren-fablesandwren?shelf=02-stars">02-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42780417-wren-fablesandwren?shelf=not-shelved">not-shelved</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1458296831" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4649678096371985750">I don't know how to review this book. It wasn't the best thing I have ever read, but with my emotions all mixed up and my health not being as it should be right now, this book straight up made me cry for what I yearn for: love.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511141888ra/24486064.gif' alt='' width='350' height='167' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Ever since I was little, I have fallen in love with the ideas of mermaids (or sirens, as some have called them). They are beautiful and mythical and quite honestly the root of my obsession of fantasy novels and movies. Anyone who knows me knows that, even though I am a poo</span>
  <span id="freeText4649678096371985750" style="display:none">I don't know how to review this book. It wasn't the best thing I have ever read, but with my emotions all mixed up and my health not being as it should be right now, this book straight up made me cry for what I yearn for: love.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511141888ra/24486064.gif" alt="" width="350" height="167" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ever since I was little, I have fallen in love with the ideas of mermaids (or sirens, as some have called them). They are beautiful and mythical and quite honestly the root of my obsession of fantasy novels and movies. Anyone who knows me knows that, even though I am a poor swinner, I can't get enough of the siren folklore.<br><br>So when Kiera Cass, the author of "The Selection" Series that I liked well enough, writes a book with the title "Sirens" I literally didn't even hestiate and ordered it off Amazon to keep and to hold forever. I didn't actually read it for months and months because I had so many other books to read. But with patiently waiting for Heir of Fire by Sarah J Maas, I decided to pick up this little 327 page book and I do not regret anything about it.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511141888ra/24486065.gif" alt="" width="350" height="196" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Kahlen is a siren. The ocean is her mother. She has three sisters at one time and together they are silent until the ocean calls them to sink a ship for her. The reasoning behind sinking ships and killing hundreds of people a year is because the ocean has to be able to have some to save thousands. Kahlen and her sisters absolutely hate the fact that they take lives, but the ocean promises that they will forget her after their 100 years is up and they are free to live as humans again.<br><br>Akinli runs into a mute-girl in the library and finds himself drawn to her even though he has never heard her voice. But she mysteriously vanishes after their first date until some months later when she washes up on the shore, upset and in a very fancy dress (which is strange since she is soaking wet).<br><br>After some unfortunate events, Akinli and Kahlen both end up very, very sick: both emotionally and physically. What is to blame? You'll have to read that to find out.<br><br>My heart hurt for not only these two characters, but for the sisters of Kahlen. For how can such a lovely ending be so brutal and cruel to my heart? I know that I am going through some things in real life over here, but... IDK this book was a short one in what I am used to reading but I absolutely adored it. I cry all the time in books and movies and... ever so I can't say that it is unusual but it felt different. <br><br>It is not a fast paced book. It is not a deep thinking book. It is merely a story of a siren and her mother the ocean. If you need a break from your war-fighting, heart thumping books, this 327 paged book is for you. It's a slow burn for sure.<br><br>I'm not one for romantic books and I still liked this book. I am so happy I bought and I am keeping this book.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer748495261515181253"><br/>I hate to say this but even though the book wasn’t really bad, it wasn’t anything much else either. In other words, it was simply meh. Actually in retrospect, it was kind of bad. Just kind of. I couldn’t wait to finish it not because it’s compelling or anything. I just wanted to be over with it which I wasn’t expecting to be feeling because despite the <i>Selection Series</i> being a cheesy fairytale dystopia, I found the writing gripping and it’s why I liked it. I’m sad to say that that was a missing </span>
  <span id="freeText748495261515181253" style="display:none"><br />I hate to say this but even though the book wasn’t really bad, it wasn’t anything much else either. In other words, it was simply meh. Actually in retrospect, it was kind of bad. Just kind of. I couldn’t wait to finish it not because it’s compelling or anything. I just wanted to be over with it which I wasn’t expecting to be feeling because despite the <i>Selection Series</i> being a cheesy fairytale dystopia, I found the writing gripping and it’s why I liked it. I’m sad to say that that was a missing ingredient here in Ms. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2987125.Kiera_Cass" title="Kiera Cass" rel="nofollow noopener">Kiera Cass</a>’ standalone.<br /><br />The premise is interesting enough but the totality of the parts to create a meaningful whole just failed to deliver. The dialogues and the humor were bland. The romance not very convincing which is sad since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6618272.The_Siren" title="The Siren by Kiera Cass" rel="nofollow noopener">Siren</a> is basically a romance novel attempting to disguise as an urban fantasy.<br /><br />There wasn’t any color or complexity to the writing. The span of time the story supposedly covers wasn’t well explored. There wasn’t any real conflict. The Ocean, as a powerful entity like a sort of Titan should have been formidable and respectable but its personification wasn’t too far from that of a stereotyped stage mother. Even the job of the girls as Sirens seemed pointless although I guess it has to be that way since they simply have to sing and lure people to plunge to their deaths. Perhaps, that’s the only accurate thing presented in the book. How present day Sirens would actually live. They would party all night long. Lol. <br /><br /> Gah! I’m sorry about the really negative review but at least I didn’t dnf it. That means the book is still entertaining enough to be read until the end and at it has a happy ending so yay!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer11118814791194660063">Reviewed by Samantha Clanton, aka Harlequin Twilight for TeensReadToo.com<br/><br/>After reading this story, it is taking everything in me to not totally gush; it is that good. THE SIREN is the story of Kahlen, mostly, along with her sisters and the Ocean. A siren is a singer, a singer of the Ocean. In order to maintain herself, the Ocean must feed; sirens help her to do that.<br/><br/>Kahlen and her "sisters," Marilyn and Aisling, begin the story and you find out quite a lot of how sirens and their lives work. The</span>
  <span id="freeText11118814791194660063" style="display:none">Reviewed by Samantha Clanton, aka Harlequin Twilight for TeensReadToo.com<br /><br />After reading this story, it is taking everything in me to not totally gush; it is that good. THE SIREN is the story of Kahlen, mostly, along with her sisters and the Ocean. A siren is a singer, a singer of the Ocean. In order to maintain herself, the Ocean must feed; sirens help her to do that.<br /><br />Kahlen and her "sisters," Marilyn and Aisling, begin the story and you find out quite a lot of how sirens and their lives work. They are beautiful, they can live around regular humans, they can live semi-normal lives, but there's a catch - they cannot age, which means staying in one place for more than a few years isn't possible, and they cannot, under any circumstances, speak, laugh, scream, or make a sound outside of a sigh or breath around a human person.<br /><br />There can be no more than four sirens at a time, and not everyone will choose to live the lives that these girls have agreed to. Their sentence is 100 years, after which the Ocean will return them and they will become normal again, and begin aging from whatever age they are frozen into (almost sounds like a dream come true at times). With only their "sisters" for company, it can become lonely, and for Kahlen that causes daydreams. That is, until one day while sitting on the beach she meets a man. He is beautiful, sad, lonely, in pain, and yet there is something about him that Kahlen can't let go.<br /><br />The Ocean warns Kahlen that no matter what happens, those must stay daydreams and she cannot chance their secret by letting her fantasies run away with her. Kahlen decides she wants to make a difference and takes up sign language, which transforms into spending a few years at schools for the deaf teaching children, and later teenagers, that being deaf isn't always a bad thing.<br /><br />Kahlen gets new "sisters," Miaka and Elizabeth, who help transform her into something better than she ever imagined she could be. Miaka is creative and she is also Kahlen's first "little sister," while Elizabeth is wild and crazy, and brings out the fun and slightly mischievous side of Kahlen. Aside from Aisling being withdrawn and bitter (think Mr. Scrooge), you don't know much about her for the most part, but she is a very important piece of Kahlen's puzzle.<br /><br />Once this human, Akinli, enters Kahlen's world, nothing else seems to mean as much. Not even the secret that she is bound to keep, and with less than 20 years left on her sentence, will it all be destroyed because of this? Now Kahlen has found the one thing she has always wanted. Is the life she could have worth destroying the life she does have? Or can she have both?<br /><br />More than anything, this is a story of love and hope. Whether that love be between sisters, family, lovers, strangers, or even love for yourself; it covers all the bases. Once I started, it was hard to stop, and I really didn't want this story to end. There were numerous parts where I actually found myself tearing up, and that never happens! Some of these situations made me want to become a siren, and then there would be a moment that broke my heart.<br /><br />Kiera Cass may be a first-time author, but I pray this is not her only book. This is truly a beautiful story all the way through. I love the imagery; it is phenomenal and almost makes you feel like you're really there (and let me tell you, there were many times in the Ocean descriptions where the song Dark Blue by Jack's Mannequin got stuck in my head. Thanks Kiera!).<br /><br />It's been a long time since I have seen a first-time author whose writing style is as beautiful as this, and she definitely has not only the talent to be a wonderful writer, but also the imagination to successfully tell a story that is not only entertaining, but also touching.<br /><br />If there was one book that I would recommend this year so far, it would be THE SIREN. Just make sure you have time on your hands, because once you start you won't be able to stop until the very end. Even then, I flipped back and forth over the final pages, hoping that there would be more magically appear before my eyes. After all, this is a fantasy! </span>
  <a data-text-id="11118814791194660063" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1655442877" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1655442877" />
    <a title="Dannii Elle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle"><img alt="Dannii Elle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508499419p2/44487975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1655442877?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dannii Elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dannii Elle" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle">Dannii Elle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062449542" href="/book/show/25944385-the-siren">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=romantic-recollections">romantic-recollections</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=fantastic-fabrications">fantastic-fabrications</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=mythological-majesty">mythological-majesty</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1655442877" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5627344945337649889">This is a retelling of the classic fairy tale, <i>The Little Mermaid</i>, and due to being fascinated and familiar with both the story and mermaid lore in general, this was a highly anticipated release for me. And, as you can probably guess from my rating, I was left a little disappointed.<br/><br/>I felt the story opened strongly. The reader is thrust straight into the heart of the action with no preamble and we oversee the death of the main protagonist's parents and her subsequent rebirth in mermaid form, all </span>
  <span id="freeText5627344945337649889" style="display:none">This is a retelling of the classic fairy tale, <i>The Little Mermaid</i>, and due to being fascinated and familiar with both the story and mermaid lore in general, this was a highly anticipated release for me. And, as you can probably guess from my rating, I was left a little disappointed.<br /><br />I felt the story opened strongly. The reader is thrust straight into the heart of the action with no preamble and we oversee the death of the main protagonist's parents and her subsequent rebirth in mermaid form, all within the first few pages. I was immediately hooked! However, the plot, whilst not at all bland, felt drawn out with long periods of little action or forward movement and it led to me feeling a total disconnect with the characters. I was enjoying the story but I wasn't <i>invested</i> in it. <br /><br />The main character, Kahlen, was likable enough but both her and her mermaid sisters seemed to fall into strict stereotypes that felt too rigid to be real. There was an inevitable love interest and an instantaneous attraction between the two that dominated much of the plot and I would have much preferred see the struggles in the family dynamic play out between these siblings of fate.<br /><br />I loved how the Ocean was addressed in the novel. She was personified as a matriarchal governing body that relied on the souls of drowned bodies. It would have been very easy for her to be cast as the villain of the story but her eternal love and nurturing of her daughters made her endearing and her cause a complex one. This also brought into question who the villain exactly was and it was interesting to see the blurring of the good/bad binaries come into play.<br /><br />Whilst not at all a bad book, I found this to be a forgettable one. It didn't gel with me, as a reader. and didn't appeal to any of my personal literary interests. Cass' writing is definitely far superior in her The Selection series than in this stand-alone and, was it not for that, I would be hesitant to read more of her work based solely on this example. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5627344945337649889" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller" href="/user/show/13396599-niki-hawkes---the-obsessive-bookseller">Niki Hawkes - The Obsessive Bookseller</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2329128910" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1449414722316657743">[4.5 stars] No one is more surprised than me how much I freaking loved this book.<br/><br/>Cass and I have a bit of a hit or miss relationship where I’m either 100% on-board fangirling… or throwing the book in disgust. Luckily, The Siren fell into the former category – something I wasn’t led to expect based on some brutal early reviews I read for the book. I have a theory as to why it caused such harsh reactions for fans of Cass’ work:<br/><br/>The book is less about the romance, where the main love interest is kep</span>
  <span id="freeText1449414722316657743" style="display:none">[4.5 stars] No one is more surprised than me how much I freaking loved this book.<br><br>Cass and I have a bit of a hit or miss relationship where I’m either 100% on-board fangirling… or throwing the book in disgust. Luckily, The Siren fell into the former category – something I wasn’t led to expect based on some brutal early reviews I read for the book. I have a theory as to why it caused such harsh reactions for fans of Cass’ work:<br><br>The book is less about the romance, where the main love interest is kept on the periphery for most of the book, and more about the relationship girl has with her sisters, mother ocean, and (most importantly) her heart. It’s a book filled to the brim with inner conflict as Kahlen struggled to come to terms with her lot in life and find her place in the world. I can see how most readers (misled by the romance-heavy nature of her previous series) might have gotten bored with the plot as it drifted further and further from the love story. As someone who is kind of sick of seeing the same recycled romance in YA, The Siren screamed to me something profoundly different and I enjoyed the shit out of it.<br><br>I think this is one I might actually want to reread. Certainly it deserves a spot in my collection (coveted and limited space at the moment). I don’t think it’s a book I could recommend with confidence because it’s a very specific, atypical YA that doesn’t fit the mold, but it definitely fit the bill as the refresh I needed in the genre.<br><br><b>Recommendations:</b> I wouldn’t recommend this necessarily for fans of Cass’ other work because it satiates an entirely different craving. Instead I’d probably hand it to the lovers of those tragic “girls in pretty dresses in a slightly dystopia era” series (which I call “elegant dystopia”). I’d also hand this to someone expressly tired with typical YA romances.<br><br>Via The Obsessive Bookseller at <a href="http://www.nikihawkes.com" rel="nofollow noopener">www.nikihawkes.com </a> <br><br>Other books you might like:<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8525590.Wither__The_Chemical_Garden___1_" title="Wither (The Chemical Garden, #1) by Lauren DeStefano" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13326831.The_Testing__The_Testing___1_" title="The Testing (The Testing, #1) by Joelle Charbonneau" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_1666509493" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1666509493" />
    <a title="Lara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39627446-lara"><img alt="Lara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498384481p2/39627446.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1666509493?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lara" href="/user/show/39627446-lara">Lara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062449542" href="/book/show/25944385-the-siren">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1666509493" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4046369503906936974"><blockquote>
  <i>“She told me to live. . . . I didn’t know how to tell Her that simply being alive was not enough to be called living.” </i>
</blockquote><br/><b><br/>Mixed feelings about this one.</b><br/><br/> This book obviously isn't as good as The Selection. But it had huge potential in it and I wish Kiera Cass used it. I liked the main idea of the book however it would be much more better if it was longer, maybe a duology?<br/> There are so many questions that re unanswered in the book. First of, why ocean eats humans? or why does she needs sinkings?<br/> </span>
  <span id="freeText4046369503906936974" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“She told me to live. . . . I didn’t know how to tell Her that simply being alive was not enough to be called living.” </i>
</blockquote><br><b><br>Mixed feelings about this one.</b><br><br> This book obviously isn't as good as The Selection. But it had huge potential in it and I wish Kiera Cass used it. I liked the main idea of the book however it would be much more better if it was longer, maybe a duology?<br> There are so many questions that re unanswered in the book. First of, why ocean eats humans? or why does she needs sinkings?<br> The ocean was pretty weird in the book, but Hers was the character with the most potential.<br>Why does sirens have to stay 100 years? They can stay less and ocean can create more sirens.<br><br> Kahlen was an okay character. There was nothing <b>wow </b>about her but she wasn't bad either.<br> Akinli was cute and sweet and I admired his ambition to keep a conversation with Kahlen even tho she can't speak.<br><b>Insta-love</b>. They were really really cute but they spend less then 24 hours together and they're soulmates!?<br> Their story could have been much more better if it was<b>LONGER</b> and better described.<br><br>Overall it was an okay read and if you're looking for something to read to kill time, you can pick this up.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1465889711ra/19411430.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br></span>

<div id="review_1551305155" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1551305155" />
    <a title="Dana Kenedy (Dana and the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/372001-dana-kenedy-dana-and-the-books"><img alt="Dana Kenedy (Dana and the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464902542p2/372001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1551305155?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dana Kenedy (Dana and the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dana Kenedy (Dana and the Books)" href="/user/show/372001-dana-kenedy-dana-and-the-books">Dana Kenedy (Dana and the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062391995" href="/book/show/25817407-the-siren">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/372001-dana-kenedy-dana-and-the-books?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/372001-dana-kenedy-dana-and-the-books?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/372001-dana-kenedy-dana-and-the-books?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/372001-dana-kenedy-dana-and-the-books?shelf=2016-release">2016-release</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1551305155" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4727294482763508111">1.5/5<br/><br/>It was my intention to write a more coherent review, but after months of not doing it I'm just pasting the notes I took while reading/directly after finishing. So I apologize for the slight stream of consciousness style review.<br/><br/>So much instalove. She met him. He was cute. They baked a cake together and of course she loves him forever and ever and can't live without him. Literally.<br/><br/>Also, Akinli's creepy candle wax burn was so ridiculously creepy. Seriously, GTFO of this book.<br/><br/>It felt more like </span>
  <span id="freeText4727294482763508111" style="display:none">1.5/5<br /><br />It was my intention to write a more coherent review, but after months of not doing it I'm just pasting the notes I took while reading/directly after finishing. So I apologize for the slight stream of consciousness style review.<br /><br />So much instalove. She met him. He was cute. They baked a cake together and of course she loves him forever and ever and can't live without him. Literally.<br /><br />Also, Akinli's creepy candle wax burn was so ridiculously creepy. Seriously, GTFO of this book.<br /><br />It felt more like a generic high school romance than a supernatural love story.<br /><br />No plot happened except Kahlen's instalove with Akinli. Then, suddenly a crisis was crammed into the remaining 40 pages. Seriously, 80% of the book is boring. Would have actually been better as a novella, not enough substance for the full 325 pages it is.<br /><br />Of course, MC falls into a depression a-la-Bella Swan for years when she can't be near him because it's just too much to be separated from her one true love that she's known for just a few hours.<br /><br />And then there's the personified Ocean who switches between talking to them like the sirens are employees and then talks to them like they're BFFs. It was pretty weird at times.<br /><br />While reading, this was hovering between 2 and 2.5 stars, but the last few pages were so worthy of eyerolling that I just had to lower the rating.<br /><br />Where was the world building? Yes, it was based in the contemporary world, but there were still elements that the reader was supposed to accept because Cass didn't bother to explain it at all. How did the sirens originate? How did they come to be? It felt like the author didn't want to look up mythology and said, "They just do, kay?"<br /><br />Would have been so much better without the romance at all. This could have been a fantastic 'girl power' story with the sirens as the focus and the dynamics of their friendship and the tragic job they must perform. The shipwreck scenes included were so brief, but they could have been so powerful. Instead, we got a creepy romance at the forefront with two dimensional supporting sirens in the background. Padma's story could have been SO good.<br /><br />The 'crisis' included just felt so out of place, so disjointed and random, that it actually took away from whatever story there actually was.<br /><br />The only positive I have is that this is a standalone and this story won't be dragged on any longer. The cover is also really pretty so two positives!<br /><br />Thankfully, I checked it out of my library.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4727294482763508111" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17358151459330059923">4.5 stars!!!<br/><br/>I love this book so much. This is my second time reading it this year and I'm so happy I read it again! This is a romance primarily similar to her last books (the selection series) but the plot plays a much bigger role in this story than the others.   <span id="freeText17358151459330059923" style="display:none">4.5 stars!!!<br /><br />I love this book so much. This is my second time reading it this year and I'm so happy I read it again! This is a romance primarily similar to her last books (the selection series) but the plot plays a much bigger role in this story than the others. I love seeing the main character's life as a Siren and her relationship with the Ocean who is basically her owner. <br /><br />This story doesn't get very deep in character or plot development and that's one thing where it's definitely lacking - Kiera Kass could have taken this story much farther. But regardless, it's a fast and fun read with one of my favorite endings ever. If you're in the mood for something light and fun you may really love this so I say give it a try!</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1524376978" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1524376978" />
    <a title="Kelly (Diva Booknerd)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11177071-kelly-diva-booknerd"><img alt="Kelly (Diva Booknerd)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479923328p2/11177071.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1524376978?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly (Diva Booknerd)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly (Diva Booknerd)" href="/user/show/11177071-kelly-diva-booknerd">Kelly (Diva Booknerd)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062449542" href="/book/show/25944385-the-siren">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11177071-kelly-diva-booknerd?shelf=harper-collins">harper-collins</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1524376978" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12443001815742061804">Release the gowns.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456197393ra/18201989.gif' alt='Image and video hosting by TinyPic' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The name Kiera Cass is synonymous with young adult, instant love, cliche storylines and of course ballgowns. Her Selection series covers are absolutely stunning and considering the predicament her protagonist America finds herself in, are well suited to the storyline and a great representation. Her novels are perfect for early teen readers who love a fairytale romance. The Siren on the other hand managed to weave underwater ballgowns into the storyline and although I enjoyed it</span>
  <span id="freeText12443001815742061804" style="display:none">Release the gowns.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456197393ra/18201989.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The name Kiera Cass is synonymous with young adult, instant love, cliche storylines and of course ballgowns. Her Selection series covers are absolutely stunning and considering the predicament her protagonist America finds herself in, are well suited to the storyline and a great representation. Her novels are perfect for early teen readers who love a fairytale romance. The Siren on the other hand managed to weave underwater ballgowns into the storyline and although I enjoyed it sporadically despite my rating, it really wasn't for me.<br><br>The storyline follows our protagonist Kahlen, pronounced Kaylynn according to Kiera Cass' Tumblr page. Kahlen was once a wealthy society girl, traveling the open seas with her parents when tragedy strikes. While those around her have perished, Kahlen is offered a lifeline. To join the sisterhood of singing Sirens or join her parents on the ocean floor. She wants to live and tentatively accepts the deal.<br><br>Fast forward eighty years and Kahlen is now a Siren, immortal and only twenty years from completing her role until another takes her place. Along with her sisters in Elizabeth, Miaka and the soon to be departed Aisling, Kahlen serves the Ocean in an emotional contract which sees her sing to to feed her thirst for human life. The Ocean is portrayed as an energy who owns the life of each Siren until her time of servitude is over. She's possessive and continues to brainwash her possessions that they are her property. Although ruling with with a firm and controlling hand, She is passive aggressive and uses the motion of Her waves to caress her Sirens to soothe them in their time of need.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456197393ra/18201990.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The Ocean has now become a third party in the strangest love triangle I've come across.<br><br>Akinli is a quiet and intelligent college student, meeting Kahlen in the student library in which he works. Apart from a name that sounds more like a cocktail, he's actually the only likable character The Siren has to offer. Like her sisters, Kahlen is mute. She communicates using sign language for the fear of her musical voice luring others to their death. Of course Akinli finds this endearing and cake baking ensues.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456197393ra/18201991.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Good times kids. Good times.<br><br>Alas, their relationship can never be and Kahlen leaves behind a heartbroken Akinli to devote herself to the Ocean once more. Absence really does make the heart grow fonder and it isn't long until Kahlen wants to return, confiding in her sisters about the absence of love of her life that is slowly destroying her spirit. If she returns to Miami, the Ocean will surely destroy the sea fairing Akinli as punishment, ensuring She has Kahlen's devotion.<br><br>That's quite the dilemma Kahlen.<br><br>What did surprise me is that The Siren isn't a new release, but a polished version of an earlier release. It had potential, but I feel the finer details of the storyline is what let The Siren down. The mythology behind the Sirens felt flimsy. Mythical beings that were said to have lured men to their deaths, their willpower stripped away and leaving girls who lacked both personality and distinguishing traits. The romance soon became the focal point of the storyline and rather than world building or introducing much needed mythology while the young loves were separated, what I found was little more than teen angst and pining away for a boy she has only just met.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456197393ra/18201992.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>#typicalcass<br><br>The overall storyline had a wonderful premise, a mythical and immortal being, a forbidden romance and obstacles to overcome. But the lack of world building, little to no character development felt as though it could have been mistaken for satire. For all it's faults and there were many many faults, I still couldn't put it down. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12443001815742061804" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
